# Task: Kubernetes client-go Systems Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce an advanced systems guide for client-go that explains API access, controller loops, and extension paths.

## Scope

Focus on the client-go subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

17-usertool_resultRead
   150→	AddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)
   151→	// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the
   152→	// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means
   153→	// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation
   154→	// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification
   155→	// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add
   156→	// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some
   157→	// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added
   158→	// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does
   159→	// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that
   160→	// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter
   161→	// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time
   162→	// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period
   163→	// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may
   164→	// be competing load and scheduling noise.
   165→	// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to remove
   166→	// the handler again and an error if the handler cannot be added.
   167→	//
   168→	// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod in code which supports contextual logging.
   169→	AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod(handler ResourceEventHandler, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)
   170→	// AddEventHandlerWithOptions is a variant of AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod where
   171→	// all optional parameters are passed in a struct.
   172→	AddEventHandlerWithOptions(handler ResourceEventHandl
... (truncated)

24-usertool_resultRead
   360→
   361→// RunWithContext repeatedly uses the reflector's ListAndWatch to fetch all the
   362→// objects and subsequent deltas.
   363→// Run will exit when the context is canceled.
   364→func (r *Reflector) RunWithContext(ctx context.Context) {
   365→	logger := klog.FromContext(ctx)
   366→	logger.V(3).Info("Starting reflector", "type", r.typeDescription, "resyncPeriod", r.resyncPeriod, "reflector", r.name)
   367→	wait.BackoffUntil(func() {
   368→		if err := r.ListAndWatchWithContext(ctx); err != nil {
   369→			r.watchErrorHandler(ctx, r, err)
   370→		}
   371→	}, r.backoffManager, true, ctx.Done())
   372→	logger.V(3).Info("Stopping reflector", "type", r.typeDescription, "resyncPeriod", r.resyncPeriod, "reflector", r.name)
   373→}
   374→
   375→var (
   376→	// Used to indicate that watching stopped because of a signal from the stop
   377→	// channel passed in from a client of the reflector.
   378→	errorStopRequested = errors.New("stop requested")
   379→)
   380→
   381→// resyncChan returns a channel which will receive something when a resync is
   382→// required, and a cleanup function.
   383→func (r *Reflector) resyncChan() (<-chan time.Time, func() bool) {
   384→	if r.resyncPeriod == 0 {
   385→		// nothing will ever be sent down this channel
   386→		return nil, func() bool { return false }
   387→	}
   388→	// The cleanup function is required: imagine the scenario where watches
   389→	// always fail so we end up listing frequently. Then, if we don't
   390→	// manually stop the timer, we could end up with many timers active
   391→	// concurrently.
   392→	t := r.clock.NewTimer(r.resyncPeriod)
   393→	return t.C(), t.Stop
   394→}
   395→

   39

    27→// Deprecated: Interface is deprecated, use TypedInterface instead.
    28→type Interface TypedInterface[any]
    29→
    30→type TypedInterface[T comparable] interface {
    31→	Add(item T)
    32→	Len() int
    33→	Get() (item T, shutdown bool)
    34→	Done(item T)
    35→	ShutDown()
    36→	ShutDownWithDrain()
    37→	ShuttingDown() bool
    38→}
    39→
    40→// Queue is the underlying storage for items. The functions below are always
    41→// called from the same goroutine.
    42→type Queue[T comparable] interface {
    43→	// Touch can be hooked when an existing item is added again. This may be
    44→	// useful if the implementation allows priority change for the given item.
    45→	Touch(item T)
    46→	// Push adds a new item.
    47→	Push(item T)
    48→	// Len tells the total number of items.
    49→	Len() int
    50→	// Pop retrieves an item.
    51→	Pop() (item T)
    52→}

    21→// RateLimitingInterface is an interface that rate limits items being added to the queue.
    22→//
    23→// Deprecated: Use TypedRateLimitingInterface instead.
    24→type RateLimitingInterface TypedRateLimitingInterface[any]
    25→
    26→// TypedRateLimitingInterface is an interface that rate limits items being added to the queue.
    27→type TypedRateLimitingInterface[T comparable] interface {
    28→	TypedDelayingInterface[T]
    29→
    30→	// AddRateLimited adds an item to the workqueue after the rate limiter says it's ok
    31→	AddRateLimited(item T)
    32→
    33→	// Forget indicates that an item is finished being retried.  Doesn't matter whether it's for perm failing
    34→	// or for success, we'll stop the rate limiter from tracking it.  This only clears the `rateLimiter`, you
    35→	// still have to call `Done` on the queue.
    36→	Forget(item T)
    37→
    38→	// NumRequeues returns back how many times the item was requeued
    39→	NumRequeues(item T) int
    40→}
    41→

   407→// `*sharedIndexInformer` implements SharedIndexInformer and has three
   408→// main components.  One is an indexed local cache, `indexer Indexer`.
   409→// The second main component is a Controller that pulls
   410→// objects/notifications using the ListerWatcher and pushes them into
   411→// a DeltaFIFO --- whose knownObjects is the informer's local cache
   412→// --- while concurrently Popping Deltas values from that fifo and
   413→// processing them with `sharedIndexInformer::HandleDeltas`.  Each
   414→// invocation of HandleDeltas, which is done with the fifo's lock
   415→// held, processes each Delta in turn.  For each Delta this both
   416→// updates the local cache and stuffs the relevant notification into
   417→// the sharedProcessor.  The third main component is that
   418→// sharedProcessor, which is responsible for relaying those
   419→// notifications to each of the informer's clients.
   420→type sharedIndexInformer struct {
   421→	indexer    Indexer
   422→	controller Controller
   423→
   424→	processor             *sharedProcessor
   425→	cacheMutationDetector MutationDetector
   426→
   427→	listerWatcher ListerWatcher
   428→
   429→	// objectType is an example object of the type this informer is expected to handle. If set, an event
   430→	// with an object with a mismatching type is dropped instead of being delivered to listeners.
   431→	objectType runtime.Object
   432→
   433→	// objectDescription is the description of this informer's objects. This typically defaults to
   434→	objectDescription string
   435→
   436→	// resyncCheckPeriod is how often we want the reflector's resync timer to fire so it can call
   437→	// should

   643→func determineResyncPeriod(logger klog.Logger, desired, check time.Duration) time.Duration {
   644→	if desired == 0 {
   645→		return desired
   646→	}
   647→	if check == 0 {
   648→		logger.Info("Warning: the specified resyncPeriod is invalid because this shared informer doesn't support resyncing", "desired", desired)
   649→		return 0
   650→	}
   651→	if desired < check {
   652→		logger.Info("Warning: the specified resyncPeriod is being increased to the minimum resyncCheckPeriod", "desired", desired, "resyncCheckPeriod", check)
   653→		return check
   654→	}
   655→	return desired
   656→}
   657→
   658→const minimumResyncPeriod = 1 * time.Second

   661→	return s.AddEventHandlerWithOptions(handler, HandlerOptions{ResyncPeriod: &resyncPeriod})
   662→}

   830→func (p *sharedProcessor) addListener(listener *processorListener) ResourceEventHandlerRegistration {
   831→	p.listenersLock.Lock()
   832→	defer p.listenersLock.Unlock()
   833→
   834→	if p.listeners == nil {
   835→		p.listeners = make(map[*processorListener]bool)
   836→	}
   837→
   838→	p.listeners[listener] = true
   839→
   840→	if p.listenersStarted {
   841→		p.wg.Start(listener.run)
   842→		p.wg.Start(listener.pop)
   843→	}
   844→
   845→	return listener
   846→}
   847→
   848→func (p *sharedProcessor) removeListener(handle ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) error {
   849→	p.listenersLock.Lock()
   850→	defer p.listenersLock.Unlock()
   851→
   852→	listener, ok := handle.(*processorListener)
   853→	if !ok {
   854→		return fmt.Errorf("invalid key type %t", handle)
   855→	} else if p.listeners == nil {
   856→		// No listeners are registered, do nothing
   857→		return nil
   858→	} else if _, exists := p.listeners[listener]; !exists {
   859→		// Listener is not registered, just do nothing
   860→		return nil
   861→	}
   862→
   863→	delete(p.listeners, listener)
   864→
   865→	if p.listenersStarted {
   866→		close(listener.addCh)
   867→	}
   868→
   869→	return nil
   870→}

The document has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

---

## Document Overview

The guide is organized into seven sections, all grounded in specific source files from `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/`:

**Section 1 – Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies**  
Establishes what `client-go` is for, who it depends on (`k8s.io/apimachinery`, `k8s.io/api`, `k8s.io/utils`), and who depends on it (built-in controllers, operators, `controller-runtime`).

**Section 2 – Key Components and Responsibility Boundaries**  
Walks through the four main layers with concrete file references:
- *REST layer* (`rest/client.go`, `rest/request.go`, `rest/with_retry.go`) – transport, rate limiting, retry
- *Informer machinery* (`tools/cache/`) – Reflector, DeltaFIFO/RealFIFO, Store/Indexer, `sharedIndexInformer`, and `sharedProcessor`
- *Work queue* (`util/workqueue/`) – the dirty/processing triset, delaying heap, and composite rate limiter
- *Ancillary tools* – leader election, clientcmd, transport wrappers

**Section 3 – End-to-End Control Flow**  
Traces the full lifecycle: factory construction → informer startup → initial list/Replace → steady-state watch → controller reconciliation loop, with function references at each step.

**Section 4 – Failure Modes, Limits, and Tradeoffs**  
Covers watch gap/missed delete, ResourceVersion expiration, handler backpressure, processLoop serialization, resync cost, the two-layer rate limiting model, and leader election's absence of fencing guarantees.

**Section 5 – Extension Points and Risks**  
Documents `TransformFunc`, custom `ResourceEventHandler`s, custom indexers, `WrapTransport`, custom `ListerWatcher` implementations, feature gate override, and custom rate limiters – each with concrete risk 
... (truncated)

This will require a little thought\n// to make sure that we don't end up processing the same object multiple times\n// concurrently.\nfunc (c *controller) processLoop(ctx context.Context) {\n\tuseBatchProcess := false\n\tbatchQueue, ok := c.config.Queue.(QueueWithBatch)\n\tif ok && c.config.ProcessBatch != nil && clientgofeaturegate.FeatureGates().Enabled(clientgofeaturegate.InOrderInformersBatchProcess) {\n\t\tuseBatchProcess = true\n\t}\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tvar err error\n\t\t\tif useBatchProcess {\n\t\t\t\terr = batchQueue.PopBatch(c.config.ProcessBatch, PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// otherwise fallback to non-batch process behavior\n\t\t\t\t_, err = c.config.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tif errors.Is(err, ErrFIFOClosed) {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandler can handle notifications for events that\n// happen to a resource. The events are informational only, so you\n// can't return an error.  The handlers MUST NOT modify the objects\n// received; this concerns not only the top level of structure but all\n// the data structures reachable from it.\n//   - OnAdd is called when an object is added.\n//   - OnUpdate is called when an object is modified. Note that oldObj is the\n//     last known state of the object-- it is possible that several changes\n//     were combined together, so you can't use this to see every single\n//     change. OnUpdate is also called when a re-list happens, and it will\n//     get called even if nothing changed. This is useful for periodically\n//     evaluating or syncing something.\n//   - OnDelete will get the final state of the item if it is known, otherwise\n//     it will get an object of type DeletedFinalStateUnknown. This can\n//     happen if the watch is closed and misses the delete event and we don't\n//     notice the deletion until the subsequent re-list.\ntype ResourceEventHandler interface {\n\tOnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n\tOnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tOnDelete(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandlerFuncs is an adaptor to let you easily specify as many or\n// as few of the notification functions as you want while still implementing\n// ResourceEventHandler.  This adapter does not remove the prohibition against\n// modifying the objects.\n//\n// See ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs if your use needs to propagate\n// HasSynced.\ntype ResourceEventHandlerFuncs struct {\n\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{})\n\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.AddFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs is exactly like ResourceEventHandlerFuncs\n// except its AddFunc accepts the isInInitialList parameter, for propagating\n// HasSynced.\ntype ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs struct {\n\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.AddFunc(obj, isInInitialList)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// FilteringResourceEventHandler applies the provided filter to all events coming\n// in, ensuring the appropriate nested handler method is invoked. An object\n// that starts passing the filter after an update is considered an add, and an\n// object that stops passing the filter after an update is considered a delete.\n// Like the handlers, the filter MUST NOT modify the objects it is given.\ntype FilteringResourceEventHandler struct {\n\tFilterFunc func(obj interface{}) bool\n\tHandler    ResourceEventHandler\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tr.Handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n}\n\n// OnUpdate ensures the proper handler is called depending on whether the filter matches\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tnewer := r.FilterFunc(newObj)\n\tolder := r.FilterFunc(oldObj)\n\tswitch {\n\tcase newer && older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\n\tcase newer && !older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnAdd(newObj, false)\n\tcase !newer && older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\n\tdefault:\n\t\t// do nothing\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tr.Handler.OnDelete(obj)\n}\n\n// DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc checks for\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n// MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\nfunc DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj interface{}) (string, error) {\n\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n\t\treturn d.Key, nil\n\t}\n\treturn MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n}\n\n// DeletionHandlingObjectToName checks for\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n// ObjectToName.\nfunc DeletionHandlingObjectToName(obj interface{}) (ObjectName, error) {\n\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n\t\treturn ParseObjectName(d.Key)\n\t}\n\treturn ObjectToName(obj)\n}\n\n// InformerOptions configure a Reflector.\ntype InformerOptions struct {\n\t// ListerWatcher implements List and Watch functions for the source of the resource\n\t// the informer will be informing about.\n\tListerWatcher ListerWatcher\n\n\t// ObjectType is an object of the type that informer is expected to receive.\n\tObjectType runtime.Object\n\n\t// Handler defines functions that should called on object mutations.\n\tHandler ResourceEventHandler\n\n\t// ResyncPeriod is the underlying Reflector's resync period. If non-zero, the store\n\t// is re-synced with that frequency - Modify events are delivered even if objects\n\t// didn't change.\n\t// This is useful for synchronizing objects that configure external resources\n\t// (e.g. configure cloud provider functionalities).\n\t// Optional - if unset, store resyncing is not happening periodically.\n\tResyncPeriod time.Duration\n\n\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n\n\t// Indexers, if set, are the indexers for the received objects to optimize\n\t// certain queries.\n\t// Optional - if unset no indexes are maintained.\n\tIndexers Indexers\n\n\t// Transform function, if set, will be called on all objects before they will be\n\t// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will be invoked\n\t// for them.\n\t// Optional - if unset no additional transforming is happening.\n\tTransform TransformFunc\n}\n\n// NewInformerWithOptions returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n// notifications to be faulty.\nfunc NewInformerWithOptions(options InformerOptions) (Store, Controller) {\n\tvar clientState Store\n\tif options.Indexers == nil {\n\t\tclientState = NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n\t} else {\n\t\tclientState = NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, options.Indexers)\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n}\n\n// NewInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n// notifications to be faulty.\n//\n// Parameters:\n//   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\n//     be informed of.\n//   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\n//   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\n//     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\n//     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\n//     or you stop the controller).\n//   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n) (Store, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options, DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n}\n\n// NewIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a Controller for populating the index\n// while also providing event notifications. err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase SyncAll:\n\t\t\t_, ok := obj.(SyncAllInfo)\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"SyncAll did not contain SyncAllInfo: %T\", obj)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tobjs := clientState.List()\n\t\t\tfor _, obj := range objs {\n\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(obj, obj)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\tcase Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); Otherwise, each Delta is processed individually.\n//\n// Returns an error if any Delta or transaction fails. For TransactionError,\n// only successful operations trigger callbacks.\nfunc processDeltasInBatch(\n\thandler ResourceEventHandler,\n\tclientState Store,\n\tdeltas []Delta,\n\tisInInitialList bool,\n\tkeyFunc KeyFunc,\n) error {\n\t// from oldest to newest\n\ttxns := make([]Transaction, 0)\n\tcallbacks := make([]func(), 0)\n\ttxnStore, txnSupported := clientState.(TransactionStore)\n\tif objects\n\tfor _, d := range deltas {\n\t\tobj := d.Object\n\t\tswitch d.Type {\n\t\tcase Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n\t\t\t// it will only return one old object for each because items are unique\n\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n\t\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n\t\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeUpdate,\n\t\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, txn)\n\t\t\t\tcallbacks = append(callbacks, func() {\n\t\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(old, obj)\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n\t\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeAdd,\n\t\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, txn)\n\t\t\t\tcallbacks = append(callbacks, func() {\n\t\t\t\t\thandler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase Deleted:\n\t\t\ttxn := Transaction{\n\t\t\t\tType:   TransactionTypeDelete,\n\t\t\t\tObject: obj,\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\ttxns = append(txns, txn)\n\t\t\tcallbacks = append(callbacks, func() {\n\t\t\t\thandler.OnDelete(obj)\n\t\t\t})\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"Delta type %s is not supported in batch processing\", err.SuccessfulIndices {\n\t\t\tif i < len(callbacks) {\n\t\t\t\tcallbacks[i]()\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\t// formatting the error so txns doesn't escape and keeps allocated in the stack.\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"not all items in the batch successfully processed: %s\", err.Error())\n\t}\n\tfor _, callback := range callbacks {\n\t\tcallback()\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc processReplacedAllInfo(handler ResourceEventHandler, info ReplacedAllInfo, clientState Store, isInInitialList bool, keyFunc KeyFunc) error {\n\tvar deletions []DeletedFinalStateUnknown\n\ttype old})\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\treplacements = append(replacements, replacement{newObj: obj})\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\t},\n\t)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\t// Replace the client the store you want to populate\n//   - options contain the options to configure the controller\nfunc newInformer(clientState Store, options InformerOptions, keyFunc KeyFunc) Controller {\n\t// This An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n// namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n// an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n// SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n// group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n// SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n// applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n//\n// The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n// access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n// An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n// other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n//\n// A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n// by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n// machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n// the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n// consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n// prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n// particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n// then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n// eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n// state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n// service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n// absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n// selector.\n//\n// For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n// states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n// states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n// might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n// states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n//\n// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n// during `Run()`.\n//\n// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n// persistently thwart achievement).\n//\n// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n//\n// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n// into its constituent parts.\n//\n// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n// snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n// will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n//\n// A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n// update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n// added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n// stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n// after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n// additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n// client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n// local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n// SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n// update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n// update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n// corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n// and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n// For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n// delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n// object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n// that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n// and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n// created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n// rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n// need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n// field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n// notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n//\n// A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n// is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n// notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n// to something else, for example through a\n// `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n//\n// A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n// state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n// ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\ntype SharedInformer interface {\n\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n\t// different handlers.\n\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n\t// seen every item in the initial list).\n\t//\n\t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\n\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)",

Implementations should return quickly - any expensive processing\n// should be offloaded.\ntype WatchErrorHandlerWithContext func(ctx context.Context, r *Reflector, err error)\n\n// DefaultWatchErrorHandler is the default implementation of WatchErrorHandlerWithContext.\nfunc DefaultWatchErrorHandler(ctx context.Context, r *Reflector, err error) {\n\tswitch {\n\tcase isExpiredError(err):\n\t\t// Don't set LastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable - LIST call with ResourceVersion=RV already\n\t\t// has a semantic that it returns data at least as fresh as provided RV.\n\t\t// So first try to LIST with setting RV to resource version of last observed object.\n\t\tklog.FromContext(ctx).V(4).Info(\"Watch closed\", \"reflector\", r.name, \"type\", r.typeDescription, \"err\", err)\n\tcase err == io.EOF:\n\t\t// watch closed normally\n\tcase err == io.ErrUnexpectedEOF:\n\t\tklog.FromContext(ctx).V(1).Info(\"Watch closed with unexpected EOF\", \"reflector\", r.name, \"type\", r.typeDescription, \"err\", err)\n\tdefault:\n\t\tutilruntime.HandleErrorWithContext(ctx, err, \"Failed to watch\", \"reflector\", r.name, \"type\", r.typeDescription)\n\t}\n}\n\n// NewNamespaceKeyedIndexerAndReflector creates an Indexer and a Reflector\n// The indexer is configured to key on namespace\nfunc NewNamespaceKeyedIndexerAndReflector(lw ListerWatcher, expectedType interface{}, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (indexer Indexer, reflector *Reflector) {\n\tindexer = NewIndexer(MetaNamespaceKeyFunc, Indexers{NamespaceIndex: MetaNamespaceIndexFunc})\n\treflector = NewReflector(lw, expectedType, indexer, resyncPeriod)\n\treturn indexer, reflector\n}\n\n// NewReflector creates a new Reflector with its name defaulted to the closest source_file.go:line in the call stack\n// that is outside this package. Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n// except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n// Deltas already ends with a Deleted. Sync is used for periodic\n// resync events.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n// intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n// the Pop() method.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n//   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n//   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n//     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n//   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n//   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n//\n// DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n// interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n// will always return an object of type Deltas. This may be\n\t// useful if the implementation allows priority change for the given item.\n\tTouch(item T)\n\t// Push adds a new item.\n\tPush(item T)\n\t// Len tells the total number of items.\n\tLen() int\n\t// Pop retrieves an item.\n\tPop() (item T)\n}\n\n// DefaultQueue is a slice based FIFO queue.\nfunc DefaultQueue[T comparable]() Queue[T] {\n\treturn new(queue[T])\n}\n\n// queue is a slice which implements Queue.\ntype queue[T comparable] []T\n\nfunc (q *queue[T]) Touch(item T) {}\n\nfunc (q *queue[T]) Push(item T) {\n\t*q = append(*q, item)\n}\n\nfunc (q *queue[T]) Len() int {\n\treturn len(*q)\n}\n\nfunc (q *queue[T]) Pop() (item T) {\n\titem = (*q)[0]\n\n\t// The underlying array still exists and reference this object, so the object will not be garbage collected.\n\t(*q)[0] = *new(T)\n\t*q = (*q)[1:]\n\n\treturn item\n}\n\n// QueueConfig specifies optional configurations to customize an Interface.\n// Deprecated: use TypedQueueConfig instead.\ntype QueueConfig = TypedQueueConfig[any]\n\ntype TypedQueueConfig[T comparable] struct {\n\t// Name for the queue. If unnamed, the metrics will not be registered.\n\tName string\n\n\t// MetricsProvider optionally allows specifying a metrics provider to use for the queue\n\t// instead of the global provider.\n\tMetricsProvider MetricsProvider\n\n\t// Clock ability to inject real or fake clock for testing purposes.\n\tClock clock.WithTicker\n\n\t// Queue provides the underlying queue to use. It is optional and defaults to slice based FIFO queue.\n\tQueue Queue[T]\n}\n\n// New constructs a new work queue (see the package comment).\n//\n// Deprecated: use NewTyped instead.\nfunc New() *Type NewTypedWithConfig(TypedQueueConfig[T]{\n\t\tName: \"\",\n\t})\n}\n\n// NewWithConfig constructs a new workqueue with ability to\n// customize different properties.\n//\n// Deprecated: use different properties.\nfunc NewTypedWithConfig[T comparable](config TypedQueueConfig[T]) *Typed[T] {\n\treturn newQueueWithConfig(config, defaultUnfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod)\n}\n\n// NewNamed creates a new named queue.\n// Deprecated: Use NewWithConfig instead.\nfunc NewNamed(name string) *Type {\n\treturn NewWithConfig(QueueConfig{\n\t\tName: name,\n\t})\n}\n\n// newQueueWithConfig constructs a new named workqueue\n// with the ability to customize different properties for testing purposes\nfunc newQueueWithConfig[T comparable](config TypedQueueConfig[T], updatePeriod time.Duration) *Typed[T] {\n\tmetricsProvider := globalMetricsProvider\n\tif config.MetricsProvider != nil {\n\t\tmetricsProvider = config.MetricsProvider\n\t}\n\n\tif config.Clock == nil {\n\t\tconfig.Clock = clock.RealClock{}\n\t}\n\n\tif config.Queue == nil {\n\t\tconfig.Queue = DefaultQueue[T]()\n\t}\n\n\treturn newQueue(\n\t\tconfig.Clock,\n\t\tconfig.Queue,\n\t\tnewQueueMetrics[T](metricsProvider, config.Name, config.Clock),\n\t\tupdatePeriod,\n\t)\n}\n\nfunc newQueue[T comparable](c clock.WithTicker, queue Queue[T], metrics queueMetrics[T], updatePeriod time.Duration) *Typed[T] {\n\tt := &Typed[T]{\n\t\tclock:                      c,\n\t\tqueue:                      queue,\n\t\tdirty:                      sets.Set[T]{},\n\t\tprocessing:                 sets.Set[T]{},\n\t\tcond:                       sync.NewCond(&sync.Mutex{}),\n\t\tmetrics:                    metrics,\n\t\tunfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod: updatePeriod,\n\t\tstopCh:                     make(chan struct{}),\n\t}\n\n\t// Don't start the goroutine for a type of noMetrics so we don't consume\n\t// resources unnecessarily\n\tif _, ok := metrics.(noMetrics[T]); !ok {\n\t\tt.wg.Go(t.updateUnfinishedWorkLoop)\n\t}\n\n\treturn t\n}\n\nconst defaultUnfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod = 500 * time.Millisecond\n\n// Type is a work queue (see the package comment).\n// Deprecated: Use Typed instead.\ntype Type = Typed[any]\n\ntype Typed[t comparable] struct {\n\t// queue defines the order in which we will work on items. Every\n\t// element of queue should be in the dirty set and not in the\n\t// processing set.\n\tqueue Queue[t]\n\n\t// dirty defines all of the items that need to be processed.\n\tdirty sets.Set[t]\n\n\t// Things that are currently being processed are in the processing set.\n\t// These things may be simultaneously in the dirty set. When we finish\n\t// processing something and remove it from this set, we'll check if\n\t// it's in the dirty set, and if so, add it to the queue.\n\tprocessing sets.Set[t]\n\n\tcond *sync.Cond\n\n\tshuttingDown bool\n\tdrain        bool\n\n\tmetrics queueMetrics[t]\n\n\tunfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod time.Duration\n\tclock                      clock.WithTicker\n\n\t// wg manages goroutines started by the queue to allow graceful shutdown\n\t// ShutDown() will wait for goroutines to exit before returning.\n\twg sync.WaitGroup\n\n\tstopCh chan struct{}\n\t// stopOnce guarantees we only signal shutdown a single time\n\tstopOnce sync.Once\n}\n\n// Add marks item as needing processing. When the queue is shutdown new\n// items will silently be ignored and not queued or marked as dirty for\n// reprocessing.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Add(item T) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\tif q.shuttingDown {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\n\t\t// the same item is added again before it is processed, call the Touch\n\t\t// function if the queue cares about it (for e.g, reset its priority)\n\t\tif !q.processing.Has(item) {\n\t\t\tq.queue.Touch(item)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tq.metrics.add(item)\n\n\tq.dirty.Insert(item)\n\tif q.processing.Has(item) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tq.queue.Push(item)\n\tq.cond.Signal()\n}\n\n// Len returns the current queue length, for informational purposes only. You\n// shouldn't e.g. gate a call to Add() or Get() on Len() being a particular\n// value, that can't be synchronized properly.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Len() int {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\treturn q.queue.Len()\n}\n\n// Get blocks until it can return an item to be processed. If shutdown = true,\n// the caller should end their goroutine. You must call Done with item when you\n// have finished processing it.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Get() (item T, shutdown bool) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\tfor q.queue.Len() == 0 && !q.shuttingDown {\n\t\tq.cond.Wait()\n\t}\n\tif q.queue.Len() == 0 {\n\t\t// We must be shutting down.\n\t\treturn *new(T), true\n\t}\n\n\titem = q.queue.Pop()\n\n\tq.metrics.get(item)\n\n\tq.processing.Insert(item)\n\tq.dirty.Delete(item)\n\n\treturn item, false\n}\n\n// Done marks item as done processing, and if it has been marked as dirty again\n// while it was being processed, it will be re-added to the queue for\n// re-processing.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) Done(item T) {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.metrics.done(item)\n\n\tq.processing.Delete(item)\n\tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\n\t\tq.queue.Push(item)\n\t\tq.cond.Signal()\n\t} else if q.processing.Len() == 0 {\n\t\tq.cond.Signal()\n\t}\n}\n\n// ShutDown will cause q to ignore all new items added to it. Worker\n// goroutines will continue processing items in the queue until it is\n// empty and then receive the shutdown signal.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShutDown() {\n\tdefer q.wg.Wait()\n\tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n\t\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\n\t})\n\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.drain = false\n\tq.shuttingDown = true\n\tq.cond.Broadcast()\n}\n\n// ShutDownWithDrain is equivalent to ShutDown but waits until all items\n// in the queue have been processed.\n// ShutDown can be called after ShutDownWithDrain to force\n// ShutDownWithDrain to stop waiting.\n// Workers must call Done on an item after processing it, otherwise\n// ShutDownWithDrain will block indefinitely.\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShutDownWithDrain() {\n\tdefer q.wg.Wait()\n\tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n\t\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\n\t})\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\tq.drain = true\n\tq.shuttingDown = true\n\tq.cond.Broadcast()\n\n\tfor q.processing.Len() != 0 && q.drain {\n\t\tq.cond.Wait()\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) ShuttingDown() bool {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\n\treturn q.shuttingDown\n}\n\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWork() {\n\tq.cond.L.Lock()\n\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n\tif !q.shuttingDown {\n\t\tq.metrics.updateUnfinishedWork()\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWorkLoop() {\n\tt := q.clock.NewTicker(q.unfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod)\n\tdefer t.Stop()\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-t.C():\n\t\t\tq.updateUnfinishedWork()\n\t\tcase <-q.stopCh:\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n",

For example if a user wanted\n// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n//\n// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n// cluster is highly recommended. {
  "content": "# client-go: An Advanced Systems Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n`client-go` is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It sits at the intersection of every controller, operator, and internal control-plane component in the Kubernetes ecosystem. Its role is to:\n\n- Provide authenticated, rate-limited, retry-capable HTTP access to the kube-apiserver's REST API.\n- Abstract the list/watch protocol into an eventually-consistent local cache (the *informer* machinery).\n- Expose a work-queue primitive that decouples event receipt from reconciliation, enabling a well-known controller pattern.\n- Offer ancillary facilities: leader election, port forwarding, remote command execution, and structured metrics.\n\n**Upstream dependencies.** `client-go` depends on `k8s.io/apimachinery` for API object types, serializers, and the watch event protocol, and on `k8s.io/api` for the concrete Kubernetes object types. It imports `k8s.io/utils` for clock abstraction (test seam), exponential backoff, and buffer utilities.\n\n**Downstream consumers.** Every Kubernetes built-in controller (scheduler, node-controller, endpoint-slice controller, etc.) uses `client-go`. Third-party operators and `controller-runtime`-based projects sit on top of the same informer/work-queue contract. The API server itself uses `client-go` for its own internal clients when it acts as a consumer (e.g. admission webhooks with client access).\n\n**Staging location.** The authoritative source lives under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/` in the main Kubernetes repository and is published as a standalone module. All references in this document use the staging path.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Boundaries\n\nThe library divides cleanly into four layers:\n\n### 2.1 REST Layer (`rest/`)\n\nThe REST layer is the raw transport. Key files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `rest/config.go` | `Config` struct \u2013 holds credentials, QPS, burst, TLS, `WrapTransport` |\n| `rest/client.go` | `RESTClient` \u2013 root URL, rate limiter, content negotiation, `http.Client` |\n| `rest/request.go` | `Request` \u2013 fluent builder for a single HTTP call |\n| `rest/with_retry.go` | `WithRetry` interface \u2013 per-request retry policy |\n\n`RESTClient` (`rest/client.go:86`) holds an `http.Client`, a root URL, and a `flowcontrol.RateLimiter`. It provides verb-oriented factory methods (`Get()`, `Post()`, `Verb(v)`) that return a `*Request`. The `Request` object accumulates the resource path, query parameters, body, and headers, then executes the call via `Do(ctx)` or opens a watch stream via `Watch(ctx)`.\n\n`rest/config.go` exposes `DefaultQPS = 5.0` and `DefaultBurst = 10` as the built-in rate-limit knobs. QPS / Burst together feed a token-bucket rate limiter whose delay is logged when it exceeds `longThrottleLatency = 50ms` (`rest/request.go:57\u201361`).\n\n`rest/with_retry.go` defines `WithRetry`, which governs whether a failed request is retried. The default implementation backs off on 429 and 5xx responses and rewinds the request body before retrying.\n\n### 2.2 Informer Machinery (`tools/cache/`)\n\nThis is the heart of the controller pattern. It comprises five cooperating types:\n\n#### Reflector (`tools/cache/reflector.go`)\n\nThe `Reflector` owns the connection to the API server for a single resource type. It is instantiated with a `ListerWatcher` and a target `ReflectorStore`, and runs a continuous `ListAndWatchWithContext` loop (`reflector.go:408`):\n\n1. On startup (or after a watch failure), it issues a **List** call (paginated via `tools/pager`) to populate the store with an initial snapshot, recording the resulting `ResourceVersion`.\n2. If the `WatchListClient` feature gate is enabled (beta as of v1.35, `features/known_features.go:89`), it can instead open a streaming **WatchList** request that returns items as a watch stream, avoiding the full list-then-watch round trip.\n3. It then opens a `Watch` call from that `ResourceVersion`, consuming `watch.Event` objects and routing them to the store via `store.Add`, `store.Update`, `store.Delete`, or `store.Replace`.\n4. On watch termination it calls `watchErrorHandler` and restarts via an exponential back-off manager seeded at 800 ms, capped at 30 s (`reflector.go:282`).\n5. Concurrently, `startResync` fires the store's `Resync()` at the configured period, triggering re-delivery of Sync deltas for all known objects.\n\nThe watch timeout is randomized in `[minWatchTimeout, 2*minWatchTimeout]` (default 5\u201310 min) to spread load across many watchers (`reflector.go:526\u2013536`). Bookmarks (`AllowWatchBookmarks: true`) are always requested to advance `lastSyncResourceVersion` without requiring a full re-list.\n\n#### DeltaFIFO / RealFIFO (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`, `tools/cache/the_real_fifo.go`)\n\nThe `DeltaFIFO` is the staging queue between the Reflector (producer) and the controller's `processLoop` (consumer). Its defining characteristic is that it accumulates **change history** (Deltas) keyed by object identity, not just the latest state.\n\nA Delta has a type (`Added`, `Updated`, `Deleted`, `Replaced`, `Sync`) and an object. When the same object key is enqueued multiple times before the consumer pops it, the accumulator grows:\n\n```\nkey \"default/pod-a\" \u2192 [Delta{Sync, pod-a-v1}, Delta{Updated, pod-a-v2}]\n```\n\n`Pop()` dequeues an entire `Deltas` slice under lock and calls the `ProcessFunc` while still holding it. This design means the controller sees every intermediate state, never skips a change, and can detect the difference between a net-new object and an update.\n\nWhen the `InOrderInformers` feature gate is enabled (beta, on by default since v1.33 \u2013 `known_features.go:66`), the queue is a `RealFIFO` instead of `DeltaFIFO`. `RealFIFO` delivers events in strict arrival order and, when `UnlockWhileProcessingFIFO` is also enabled, releases the queue lock during `ProcessFunc` execution to allow concurrent producers to continue adding events.\n\nThe `KnownObjects` reference back to the downstream `Store` is critical: during a `Replace()` call (initial list or re-list), `DeltaFIFO` computes the symmetric difference between the listed keys and `KnownObjects.ListKeys()` to synthesize `Deleted` deltas for any objects that have vanished.\n\n#### Store / Indexer (`tools/cache/store.go`, `tools/cache/index.go`, `tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`)\n\nThe `Store` interface (`store.go:41`) is a keyed map of live objects with `Add`, `Update`, `Delete`, `List`, `Get`, `GetByKey`, `Replace`, and `Resync` methods. The concrete implementation is `cache` (lowercase, unexported), which wraps a `ThreadSafeStore`.\n\n`ThreadSafeStore` (`thread_safe_store.go:43`) couples a `sync.RWMutex`-protected object map with a `storeIndex` \u2013 the secondary index structure. An `Indexer` (`index.go:35`) extends `Store` with `Index`, `ByIndex`, `IndexKeys`, and `ListIndexFuncValues`. Callers register `IndexFunc` functions (returning a slice of string keys) under named indexes; the `NamespaceIndex` / `MetaNamespaceIndexFunc` pair is the canonical example, mapping objects to their namespace.\n\nLookups like `informer.GetIndexer().ByIndex(\"namespace\", \"kube-system\")` are O(1) set lookups, not linear scans \u2013 the store maintains an inverted index (map[indexedValue]set[storageKey]).\n\n#### sharedIndexInformer (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`)\n\n`sharedIndexInformer` (`shared_informer.go:420`) is the user-facing type. It owns three sub-components:\n\n1. **`indexer Indexer`** \u2013 the live object cache, described above.\n2. **`controller Controller`** \u2013 a low-level controller (`tools/cache/controller.go:114`) that runs the Reflector and the processLoop.\n3. **`processor *sharedProcessor`** \u2013 fan-out relay to N registered event handlers.\n\nThe controller's `ProcessFunc` is `sharedIndexInformer.HandleDeltas`, which (under a `blockDeltas` mutex) applies each delta to `indexer` then notifies the `sharedProcessor`. The mutex prevents a race between late-joining handlers (which replay the existing cache) and live delta processing.\n\n`sharedProcessor` (`shared_informer.go:803`) holds a map of `*processorListener` values. Each listener has two goroutines: `pop` drains a channel and transfers notifications to a ring-buffer (`k8s.io/utils/buffer`), and `run` drains the buffer and calls the user's `ResourceEventHandler`. This two-goroutine design decouples a slow handler from stalling the distribution path. Resync-only notifications are filtered per-listener based on each listener's `resyncPeriod`, allowing different handlers to request different resync cadences from the same underlying informer connection.\n\n#### SharedInformerFactory (`informers/factory.go`)\n\n`sharedInformerFactory` (`factory.go:57`) is a registry of one `SharedIndexInformer` per `reflect.Type`. When code calls `factory.Core().V1().Pods().Informer()`, the factory lazily constructs the informer (if absent), stores it keyed by `reflect.TypeOf(&v1.Pod{})`, and returns the shared instance. All callers that request the same type share a single Reflector and a single store, so one watch connection services all controllers interested in Pods.\n\n`factory.Start(stopCh)` (`factory.go:144`) iterates the map and starts each not-yet-started informer in its own goroutine. `WaitForCacheSync` polls `informer.HasSynced()` at 100 ms intervals until all informers report that the initial list has been processed.\n\n### 2.3 Work Queue (`util/workqueue/`)\n\nThe work queue decouples informer event delivery from the reconciliation loop. Key files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `util/workqueue/queue.go` | Base `Typed[T]` queue with deduplication |\n| `util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go` | Adds `AddAfter(item, delay)` |\n| `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go` | Adds `AddRateLimited`, `Forget`, `NumRequeues` |\n| `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go` | Built-in rate limiter implementations |\n\n`Typed[T]` (`queue.go:190`) maintains three data structures under a single mutex:\n\n- **`queue Queue[T]`** \u2013 ordered FIFO of items to be processed (no duplicates at any moment).\n- **`dirty sets.Set[T]`** \u2013 the union of queued and currently-processing items that are pending.\n- **`processing sets.Set[T]`** \u2013 items currently held by a `Get()` caller.\n\n`Add(item)` inserts into `dirty`. If the item is already in `processing`, it does not enqueue it again \u2013 instead the item remains in `dirty` and is re-enqueued when `Done(item)` is called. This guarantees that if an object changes while it is being reconciled, reconciliation runs again, but never more than once per pending change.\n\n`TypedRateLimitingInterface` (`rate_limiting_queue.go:27`) wraps a `TypedDelayingInterface` (which uses a min-heap for delayed delivery) and delegates rate decisions to a `TypedRateLimiter`. The **default rate limiter** (`default_rate_limiters.go:50`) composites two limiters via `MaxOfRateLimiter`:\n\n- `ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter`: per-item back-off starting at 5 ms, doubling on each failure, capped at 1000 s.\n- `BucketRateLimiter`: token-bucket at 10 QPS / burst 100, global across all items.\n\nThe composite means an item that fails repeatedly backs off exponentially (protecting the API server from hammering), while the global bucket prevents a large burst of distinct keys from flooding it.\n\n### 2.4 Ancillary Tools\n\n- **`tools/leaderelection/`** \u2013 distributed leader election using Kubernetes `Lease`, `ConfigMap`, or `Endpoints` objects as a lock. Tolerant of arbitrary clock skew; tunable via `LeaseDuration`, `RenewDeadline`, and `RetryPeriod` (`leaderelection.go:76\u2013101`). Provides `OnStartedLeading`, `OnStoppedLeading`, and `OnNewLeader` callbacks.\n- **`tools/clientcmd/`** \u2013 kubeconfig parsing, merging, and REST config construction from KUBECONFIG files or in-cluster service account tokens.\n- **`transport/`** \u2013 TLS configuration, exec-based credential plugins, and `WrapperFunc` chain for pluggable authentication middleware.\n- **`util/flowcontrol/`** \u2013 token-bucket `RateLimiter` used directly by `RESTClient`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\nThis section traces the full path from a Kubernetes object change to a controller reconciling it.\n\n### 3.1 Phase 1: Startup\n\n```\ncontroller binary\n  \u2514\u2500\u2500 NewSharedInformerFactory(client, resyncPeriod)   [informers/factory.go:112]\n       \u2514\u2500\u2500 factory.Core().V1().Pods().Informer()\n            \u2514\u2500\u2500 factory.InformerFor(&v1.Pod{}, newPodInformer)  [factory.go:200]\n                 \u2514\u2500\u2500 NewSharedIndexInformerWithOptions(lw, &v1.Pod{}, opts) [shared_informer.go:303]\n                      \u2514\u2500\u2500 sharedIndexInformer{\n                            indexer:    NewIndexer(MetaNamespaceKeyFunc, opts.Indexers),\n                            processor:  &sharedProcessor{},\n                            listerWatcher: lw,\n                          }\n```\n\nThe factory's `InformerFor` is idempotent \u2013 calling it twice with the same type returns the same instance.\n\n### 3.2 Phase 2: Running\n\n`factory.Start(stopCh)` spawns one goroutine per informer type: `go informer.Run(stopCh)`.\n\nInside `sharedIndexInformer.RunWithContext` (`shared_informer.go:537`):\n\n1. A `DeltaFIFO` (or `RealFIFO` if `InOrderInformers` is enabled) is created with `s.indexer` as `KnownObjects`.\n2. A `Config` is built connecting the FIFO to `HandleDeltas` as the `ProcessFunc`.\n3. A `controller` is created and run: it spawns a `Reflector.RunWithContext` goroutine and then enters `processLoop`.\n4. The `sharedProcessor.run` goroutine starts all listener goroutine pairs.\n\n### 3.3 Phase 3: Initial List\n\n`Reflector.ListAndWatchWithContext` (`reflector.go:408`) calls `r.list(ctx)`, which:\n\n1. Issues a paginated LIST (via `tools/pager`) at `ResourceVersion=\"\"` (consistent read from etcd).\n2. Calls `r.store.Replace(items, resourceVersion)` on the DeltaFIFO.\n3. `DeltaFIFO.Replace` computes deletion deltas for objects in `KnownObjects` not in the list, then enqueues `Replaced` deltas for all listed objects.\n\n`processLoop` pops each `Deltas` slice and calls `HandleDeltas`, which in turn calls `processDeltas` (`controller.go:581`). For each delta of type `Replaced`/`Added`:\n\n- If the object exists in `indexer`: call `indexer.Update(obj)` then `handler.OnUpdate(old, obj)`.\n- Otherwise: call `indexer.Add(obj)` then `handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList=true)`.\n\n`sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd` calls `processor.distribute(addNotification{...}, false)`, which fans out to every `processorListener.add(...)`. Each listener's `pop` goroutine buffers the notification; `run` drains the buffer and calls the user's `ResourceEventHandler.OnAdd`.\n\nAfter all `Replace` deltas are processed, `controller.HasSynced()` returns `true`, unblocking any `WaitForCacheSync` callers.\n\n### 3.4 Phase 4: Steady-State Watch\n\nAfter the initial list, the Reflector opens a Watch at the recorded `ResourceVersion`. Incoming `watch.Event` objects are converted to `Add`, `Update`, or `Delete` calls on the DeltaFIFO. The processLoop handles them identically to phase 3, except `isInInitialList=false`.\n\nWatch events carry the object's new ResourceVersion. The Reflector advances `lastSyncResourceVersion` on every event, ensuring the next watch or re-list starts from the correct point.\n\n### 3.5 Phase 5: Controller Reconciliation\n\nTypical controller code uses the informer-to-work-queue bridge:\n\n```go\ninformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n        key, _ := cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n        queue.Add(key)\n    },\n    UpdateFunc: func(_, new interface{}) { ... },\n    DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) { ... },\n})\n```\n\nThe reconcile loop calls `queue.Get()` (blocks until an item is available), runs the reconcile function, then calls `queue.Done(key)`. If reconciliation fails, the controller calls `queue.AddRateLimited(key)` instead of `queue.Forget(key)`, which causes the item to be re-enqueued after an exponential back-off delay.\n\nThe key design insight: the controller reads the **current state from the informer's local cache** (via `lister.Pods(ns).Get(name)`), not from the API server. This eliminates per-reconcile API calls and provides a consistent snapshot.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Watch Gap / Missed Delete\n\nIf the watch connection drops and the Reflector misses a delete event before reconnecting, `DeltaFIFO.Replace()` detects the gap during re-list: the deleted object is in `KnownObjects` but not in the new list, so a `Deleted` delta with `DeletedFinalStateUnknown` is synthesized. Handlers receiving `OnDelete` with this type must be prepared for stale object state (`controller.go:261\u2013263`).\n\n### 4.2 ResourceVersion Expiration\n\nEtcd compacts its event history. If the Reflector's `lastSyncResourceVersion` has been compacted away, the watch returns `HTTP 410 Gone`. `DefaultWatchErrorHandler` catches `isExpiredError` and lets `ListAndWatchWithContext` fall back to a full re-list from `ResourceVersion=\"\"`. This is transparent to consumers but causes a brief latency spike.\n\n### 4.3 Handler Backpressure\n\n`SharedInformer` comment at `shared_informer.go:136` explicitly warns: *\"A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of notifications to deliver.\"* Each `processorListener` has an unbounded ring buffer (`k8s.io/utils/buffer`). A slow handler causes memory to grow without bound. The intended pattern is to enqueue only a key into a work queue and do no non-trivial work in the handler.\n\n### 4.4 processLoop Serialization\n\nThe controller's `processLoop` (`controller.go:221`) calls `Pop()` sequentially. The comment at line 219 notes this explicitly: *\"TODO: Consider doing the processing in parallel.\"* For informers with high event rates, the single-threaded processLoop can become a bottleneck. `InOrderInformersBatchProcess` (beta, on by default as of v1.35) addresses this by batching multiple `Delta` values into a single `PopBatch` call, reducing lock overhead.\n\n### 4.5 Resync Cost\n\nResync delivers synthetic `OnUpdate` calls for every cached object, even if nothing changed. For informers caching tens of thousands of objects, this can produce a burst of reconcile work. Setting the resync period to zero (`0`) disables it entirely; when non-zero, the minimum enforced period is 1 second (`shared_informer.go:658`).\n\n### 4.6 Rate Limiting and the Two-Layer Model\n\n`client-go` applies rate limiting at two distinct levels:\n\n1. **RESTClient level** (`rest/config.go`): token-bucket on all outgoing HTTP requests (default 5 QPS / burst 10). This protects the API server from any single client.\n2. **Work queue level** (`util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go`): per-item exponential back-off composited with a global token bucket. This throttles *reconcile retries*, not raw API calls.\n\nThe two levels are independent. A controller that issues many API calls per reconcile can still exceed the RESTClient rate limit. Setting `QPS` and `Burst` in `rest.Config` must be calibrated to the expected reconcile frequency and the number of API calls per reconcile.\n\n### 4.7 Leader Election Guarantees\n\nThe leader election implementation (`tools/leaderelection/`) explicitly warns in its package comment that it *\"does not guarantee that only one client is acting as a leader\"* (no fencing token). Under severe clock skew or GC pauses, two instances can briefly believe they hold the lease. Applications that need strict mutual exclusion must implement external fencing (e.g., etcd's optimistic concurrency or resource-version checks).\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 5.1 `TransformFunc` \u2013 Store Preprocessing\n\n`SharedInformer.SetTransform(TransformFunc)` (`shared_informer.go:232`) registers a function called on every object before it is stored in the local cache. The common use case is stripping fields that consume memory but are never needed by the controller (e.g., managed fields, last-applied annotation). Must be set before `Run()`.\n\n**Risk:** The transform is called in the processLoop goroutine under the DeltaFIFO lock. A slow or panicking transform blocks all event processing. Mutations made to the object in place will corrupt the cache and can cause subtle bugs; the function must return a new object or operate on a deep copy.\n\n### 5.2 `ResourceEventHandler` \u2013 Event Callbacks\n\n`AddEventHandler` / `AddEventHandlerWithOptions` registers callbacks for add/update/delete. Multiple handlers can be registered on a single informer. The `FilteringResourceEventHandler` adapter (`controller.go:339`) applies a predicate before dispatching.\n\n**Risk:** Handlers must not modify the objects they receive \u2013 the shared cache stores pointers, and mutations affect all other consumers of the same informer. The `MutationDetector` (`tools/cache/mutation_detector.go`) is a debug-mode facility that deep-copies objects and compares them periodically; enable it in tests by setting `KUBE_CACHE_MUTATION_DETECTOR=true`.\n\n### 5.3 Custom Indexers\n\n`AddIndexers(Indexers)` (`shared_informer.go:624`) can be called before the informer is started to add secondary indexes. This enables efficient lookups like \"all pods in namespace X with label Y\" via `ByIndex`.\n\n**Risk:** Index functions are called synchronously in the store's write path. An O(n) index function on large objects will amplify every event's processing cost. Indexes cannot be removed once added.\n\n### 5.4 `WrapTransport` \u2013 HTTP Middleware\n\n`rest/config.go:115` exposes `WrapTransport transport.WrapperFunc`, which layeres a `http.RoundTripper` on top of the base transport. This is the hook for custom authentication, tracing, metrics, and retry middleware.\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect middleware can break retries (by consuming the body), introduce request ordering dependencies, or silently swallow errors. Middleware added via `WrapTransport` runs before the client's rate limiter.\n\n### 5.5 `ListerWatcher` \u2013 Custom Data Sources\n\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface (`tools/cache/listwatch.go:38,66`) can be implemented to back an informer from any list/watch source, not just the API server. This is how `controller-runtime`'s dynamic informers and webhook-backed caches are built.\n\n**Risk:** The Reflector makes assumptions about the `ResourceVersion` semantics of returned objects. Custom implementations that do not honor monotonically increasing resource versions will cause the Reflector to loop in re-list or fail to detect updates.\n\n### 5.6 Feature Gates \u2013 Runtime Behavioral Switches\n\n`features/features.go` exposes `ReplaceFeatureGates(Gates)` for embedding binaries to plug in their own feature gate implementation (e.g., kube-controller-manager's component-base gate). This allows the same client-go code path to participate in the cluster's global feature flag system.\n\n**Risk:** `ReplaceFeatureGates` must be called before any informer is constructed. If called after feature gates have been read (e.g., after the first informer starts), a warning is emitted and behavior may be inconsistent (`features.go:129`).\n\n### 5.7 Custom Rate Limiters\n\nThe `TypedRateLimiter` interface is open for extension. A custom limiter can implement priority-based scheduling (e.g., process CRD updates before status updates) or integrate with an external admission controller's token service.\n\n**Risk:** Returning a very large `When()` value from a rate limiter causes items to stall in the delaying queue's min-heap indefinitely. Failing to call `Forget(item)` after success leaks per-item failure counters, causing ever-increasing delays for future occurrences of the same key.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Memory Footprint\n\nEach informer holds an in-memory copy of every object of its type. For high-cardinality resources (Pods, Endpoints, EndpointSlices), this is the dominant memory consumer in controllers. Mitigation options:\n\n- **`TransformFunc`**: strip unused fields before storage. Dropping `metadata.managedFields` and `metadata.annotations[\"kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration\"]` can halve the per-object footprint.\n- **Field/Label selectors via `WithTweakListOptions`** (`factory.go:87`): narrow the informer's scope at the API server, reducing the number of objects transferred and cached.\n- **`WithNamespace`** (`factory.go:95`): restrict to a single namespace when cross-namespace visibility is not needed.\n\n### 6.2 API Server Connection Count\n\nEach distinct `SharedIndexInformer` maintains one long-lived watch connection to the API server. A factory with N resource types opens N watch connections. At scale (many controllers, many resource types), this can exhaust API server connection limits. Prefer the `SharedInformerFactory` over constructing informers directly; it enforces one informer per type per factory instance.\n\n### 6.3 Startup Latency and `HasSynced`\n\nControllers must wait for `WaitForCacheSync` before processing work-queue items. This blocks until every informer has completed its initial list. For clusters with millions of objects, the initial list is paginated and can take 10\u201330 seconds. The `WatchListClient` feature gate (`known_features.go:89`, beta default-on since v1.35) replaces the initial list with a streaming watch, which can significantly reduce startup latency on high-object-count clusters.\n\n### 6.4 Resync Tuning\n\nSetting a non-zero `defaultResync` on the factory causes all informers to periodically re-deliver every cached object as `OnUpdate` events. If 50,000 Pods exist and the resync period is 30 seconds, controllers receive 50,000/30 \u2248 1,667 reconcile triggers per second at steady state just from resyncs, even with no actual changes. For controllers whose reconciliation is purely event-driven, set resync to 0.\n\n### 6.5 Work Queue Observability\n\nNamed queues emit Prometheus metrics (queue depth, add rate, processing latency, unfinished work) via the `MetricsProvider` interface (`util/workqueue/metrics.go`). Unnamed queues (constructed via `workqueue.New()` without a name) do not emit metrics. Always name production queues via `TypedQueueConfig.Name`.\n\nThe `unfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod` (500 ms by default) drives a goroutine that periodically updates the `workqueue_unfinished_work_seconds` gauge. A growing unfinished-work metric indicates a reconcile loop that is taking too long or is deadlocked.\n\n### 6.6 CBOR Wire Format\n\n`features/known_features.go:49-60` shows `ClientsAllowCBOR` and `ClientsPreferCBOR` (alpha as of v1.32). When enabled, `client-go` negotiates CBOR encoding with the API server instead of JSON. CBOR is more compact and faster to decode for large objects. These gates are off by default; operators should not enable them in production until the API server's CBOR support stabilizes.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File Map\n\nThe following are the most important files for understanding `client-go`'s behavior, as used in this analysis:\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/client-go/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 features/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 features.go              # FeatureGates interface, ReplaceFeatureGates, envvar implementation\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 known_features.go        # All client-go feature gate constants and default values\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 informers/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 factory.go               # SharedInformerFactory: registry, Start, WaitForCacheSync, InformerFor\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 rest/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 client.go                # RESTClient: base URL, rate limiter, verb factories\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 config.go                # Config struct: credentials, QPS, Burst, WrapTransport, Timeout\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 request.go               # Request: fluent builder, Do, Watch, Stream execution\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 with_retry.go            # WithRetry interface; per-request retry/backoff policy\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 tools/cache/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 controller.go            # Controller interface; processLoop; ResourceEventHandler types;\n\u2502   \u2502                            # FilteringResourceEventHandler; processDeltas; processDeltasInBatch\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 delta_fifo.go            # DeltaFIFO: accumulator queue; Replace; Resync; KnownObjects\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 index.go                 # Indexer interface; IndexFunc; NamespaceIndex constant\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 listwatch.go             # ListerWatcher, ListerWatcherWithContext interfaces\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 reflector.go             # Reflector: ListAndWatchWithContext; watch; backoff; WatchErrorHandler\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 shared_informer.go       # SharedInformer/SharedIndexInformer interfaces;\n\u2502   \u2502                            # sharedIndexInformer; sharedProcessor; processorListener;\n\u2502   \u2502                            # HandleDeltas; WaitForCacheSync\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 store.go                 # Store interface; Transaction types; TransactionStore\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 thread_safe_store.go     # ThreadSafeStore; storeIndex; inverted index implementation\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 tools/leaderelection/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 leaderelection.go        # LeaderElector; LeaseDuration/RenewDeadline/RetryPeriod semantics\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 util/workqueue/\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 default_rate_limiters.go # DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter; ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter;\n    \u2502                            # BucketRateLimiter; Add/Get/Done/ShutDown\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 rate_limiting_queue.go   # TypedRateLimitingInterface; AddRateLimited; Forget; NumRequeues\n```\n",
